Editorial Office

A Few Words to Offer to Husbands 213

— Jin Ling

After unfolding the October 31st newspaper and reading Chairman Chiang's "Reflections on My Fiftieth Birthday," many thoughts immediately emerged in my mind. I feel how important the responsibility of a mother is. In today's society, even though there is talk of gender equality, it has not actually been achieved. However, we should never be pessimistic or despondent due to the bad habits of valuing men over women passed down through generations.

A few days ago, we gathered at a friend's house and talked about the state of our family life and what our husbands were like. Some were animated, while others were unremarkable. When it came to Mrs. C, she frowned deeply, looking very sad! I am very familiar with her situation. She is a woman who received a good education. She has been married for five and a half years, but she is about to become the mother of her fifth child. Her husband works in a certain place, and they spend very little time together. Her husband is also a well-educated person. The slogans he shouts are "Renovation" and "Revolution." In reality, he is full of corrupt ideas, is stubborn and inflexible. He only returns home three or four times a year. He has no comfort for this gentle and hardworking wife, and he doesn't express any affection. He only treats his wife as a servant, and he always says things that pierce the heart: "Women? What are women good for? Except to be used by men as a source of pleasure." He also dislikes her for having too many children, for losing her beauty as a woman, for not having charm, coquettishness, or anything else. In his eyes, a 26- or 27-year-old woman has aged beyond recognition, so he often complains about her and hates her. In this situation, what joy does C have in life? What courage to move forward and what hope for a bright future? She has been working hard for her children, raising the children she has already given birth to and caring for the unborn fetus. In a family with limited financial resources, she tries her best to save money and manages the housework in an orderly manner. Because of excessive childbearing, she has indeed lost her health. After all her hard work, she hopes to get some comfort from her husband, like a withered branch waiting for irrigation. But what are the results she gets? Bitter tears; feelings of grief and indignation; Her experience almost made her determined to commit suicide. But when she looks back at this group of children who are crying and waiting to be fed, how can she bear to embark on this dead end? While sympathizing with her pain, I often advise her: "Everyone has their own responsibilities. No matter how difficult the situation, you have to be patient. The responsibility of raising these children is too great. You shouldn't sacrifice your own life for him alone and abandon your task as a 'person.'"

Writing this, I have a few words to offer to the husbands in general: A harmonious family is not created simply by the wife's obedience, docility, adherence to chastity, and not crossing the line. Husbands should also abide by the morals that people should have, and they should not naturally submit to fierce women. When they meet gentle women, they bully them in every possible way, do whatever they want, regardless of everything, thinking that in the era of male power, women's status is not worth mentioning. Wives, of course, also have conditions that should be observed. "Cultivating one's character, managing one's household, governing one's country, and bringing peace to the world" - the family is the foundation of society. Wives bear the heavy responsibility of managing the family and raising children, which is not a trivial matter. Husbands should encourage their wives, comfort them, and allow them to wholeheartedly strive for the sake of the family. It is not right to hold that self-deprecating mentality, to be tyrannical, exaggerated, and to exercise unreasonable patriarchal power in the home. If husband and wife respect and love each other, wouldn't there be fewer shortcomings in the family?

Persecution Suffered by Modern Professional Women (Part 2) 214

— Li Shouzhen

Secondly, female teachers in general schools, female staff in institutions, and female office workers in various professional sectors often cannot do more important work based on their abilities. In an institution, when the same work is assigned to two employees of equal status, the work given to the male employee is always more important than that given to the female employee. Is this a special favor for women? This is merely a kind of insult that belittles women's abilities or a means of suppressing women's development. Their employment of female staff is not from the standpoint of using talent, but to use them as mere ornaments. People slander the female staff of various institutions as "vases." Is it that women willingly become vases? It's just a bunch of bored men using their despicable mentality to insult women.

What's worse is that when a young woman with thoughts and a mind has just stepped through the door of society, she receives a love letter from the east, a request from the west, a bunch of annoying entanglements, and a shameless smile from the west. Those with willpower struggle all day long, constantly angry, and try to eliminate these dirty deeds by all means. As a result, they cannot move forward quickly in their careers and find it difficult to develop their future quickly. And what about those who are a little weaker in willpower? They eventually give in to the harassment. Then a group of men shout that women are useless, scold them for being depraved, and slander their purpose of seeking work and careers. In this way, many fathers and brothers use this to suppress their daughters and sisters, and they slander other people's daughters and sisters, so that their fathers and brothers also suppress them in the same way.

Thus, we can see the treatment that modern women receive and the contemptible cruelty of society towards professional women.

Now, I hope that our female compatriots deeply understand their position and their personality, and summon their courage and perseverance. As long as we can recognize that we are individuals, then we cannot retreat because of the persecution of others and fail to fulfill our obligations as human beings. The stronger the external pressure on us, the greater our resistance should be. We should not take those persecuting facts as great pressure. We should look at those few compatriots who have struggled out from severe oppression. As long as we have determination and courage and do not accept people's hypocritical charity, but do as much work as we can with our own ability and get as much benefit as we can, people will lose the opportunity to humiliate us and will have no excuse to slander us. Even if they want to suppress us in any way, it is impossible. Female compatriots! Never give in, never compromise, never retreat. One day, society will realize how foolish and inhumane their past persecution of women was and realize that mutual respect and mutual help are the virtues that human beings should have!

Private Secretary (Part 2) 215

— Xueying

That evening, Shao Yi arrived home at approximately 9:45 PM. Her father was sitting alone on the sofa downstairs, seemingly waiting for her return. Since that evening when Shao Yi argued with her father, she hadn't spoken properly to him, only greeting him briefly when they met. At this moment, with no one else in the downstairs living room, her father couldn't help but speak first:

"Of course, I support you working, but girls are not like boys, and you need to be more careful when finding a job. Where are you working now?"

Shao Yi, of course, could no longer ignore this question and gave a brief explanation, not mentioning at all how the Mr. □ invited her to the theatre or dinner, nor even that there were only two of them in the room. Her father felt much relieved when he heard it was a miscellaneous journal, and he added a few words in his usual condescending tone, nothing more than telling her to come home early, not to socialize with people casually, and to be frugal in her dress.

When Shao Yi was resting alone in bed, she felt her mind filled with many strange thoughts that she had never had before. And at the center of these thoughts was always the Mr. □. Although her father's words were still ringing in her ears, they had very little power. She did not believe that this kind of socializing that arose from work would have any significant consequences. She understood the Mr. □'s strange attitude, thinking it was the usual courtesy that employers showed to a private secretary, with the aim of stimulating her loyalty to her job.

The next day, in the overly opulent New Moon Magazine office, the Mr. □ told her that he hoped she could keep all business, writing, and social secrets, while focusing on her work. He would give her long-term preferential treatment and increase her salary in three months. This dispelled some of the doubts that Shao Yi had initially harbored, and that afternoon, he solemnly instructed Shao Yi to write three English letters, officially starting her work.

The work of a private secretary proceeded smoothly, and the various courtesies Shao Yi received increased day by day. In addition to her regular monthly salary, he also gave her clothing materials, gloves, watches, and so on, almost exceeding her salary by five or ten times. But Shao Yi did not find it strange. She gradually developed a misconception that a "private secretary" was the closest friend, so she believed that Bao Rong—that is, Mr. □—should treat her like this, and she should enjoy it.

A month, two months, passed quickly. Although her father had become suspicious of many aspects of her dress and behavior, and had questioned her several times, she always fobbed him off with various lies, faithfully keeping all secrets for her employer. Her father had no choice but to sigh angrily for a while.

Later, the misconception that a private secretary was the closest friend evolved into the fact that a private secretary was a secret lover. Shao Yi felt that Bao Rong was really too good to her, and that just working for him was not enough to repay him, so she gave him all the comfort he asked for. And Bao Rong's economy was extremely unusually abundant, and without much effort, he moved the New Moon Magazine office to YuYuan Road, expanding it into an extremely modern new home, openly cohabiting with his private secretary.

Since things were like this, Shao Yi's father could no longer criticize them, and he made a very simple request, which was to urge them to quickly hold a wedding ceremony. Shao Yi repeatedly urged Bao Rong about this, but Bao Rong prevaricated in every way, and also inadvertently revealed many loopholes that he already had a "wife at home." Shao Yi remembered many of the things her father had asked her before, as well as the various lies she herself had told, and really felt she had no face to tell her father again, and could only try to endure it, until her first son was born in the hospital, and she was still a "private secretary" to Bao Rong, with no legitimate status.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Nine Flowers Mountain Netherworld Bell 216

— Wen

From the newspaper, I saw a very large advertisement, the Netherworld Bell on the top of Jiuhua Mountain, will be cast on December 30th, the birthday of Amitabha Buddha. This is the only huge bell in our country. The preparation time, it is said, has been two or three years, the weight is more than ten tons, when struck, the sound can be heard within a hundred miles. Our country lags behind others in everything. Now there is this huge bell, which can also be called a "most" in the international arena. Compared with the United States' fondness for calling itself "first," it is really not ashamed. How can it not be called a national event!

I have considered the purpose of the Netherworld Bell. It is to startle the countless ghosts of the netherworld with its grand sound, so that they can quickly awaken, turn back to the shore, and ascend to the Western Paradise. In my hometown, if a woman dies due to childbirth, her husband or children must ask the temple to strike this bell for seven days and nights. It is said that if they don't do so, the dead ghost will be forever trapped in the "pool of blood and filth" and will not be able to transcend. When striking the bell, a large oil tank is placed under the bell, with rush lights lit, floating on the oil. Above it hangs a paper-扎 woman, with disheveled hair, looking extremely terrifying. Watching the oil fire flicker, listening to the faint bell sound, being there in person, shuddering, one truly feels like they have arrived in the netherworld. Besides this, I have not seen it struck for other things. It seems that the temple's preparation of the Netherworld Bell is specifically for awakening the women in the netherworld who have died due to childbirth. Now, the various great philanthropists and Buddhist disciples in the country have made a grand vow to cast this huge bell on the top of Jiuhua Mountain, and its meaning is naturally different.

Counting on my fingers, in the past ten years, how many people in our country have died in internal wars? How many have died under the enemy's slaughter? How many have died in droughts and floods? And how many have died in unclear, dark massacres? If hell really exists, I am afraid that hell is also full. Gathering these countless ghosts, in the gate of hell, they will not be very peaceful. If Yama really exists, I am afraid he will sigh that it is difficult to govern. Now there is a huge bell, with its grand sound, faintly reaching directly to the ground, the ghosts will hear it and their bones will soften and their muscles will become weak. Yama can then calmly send them away, saying: "Each of you go to the Western Paradise, do not linger here, creating trouble"! Thus, the ghost world can achieve peace.

Noble Old Man 217

— Lin Na

Every time I pass through that square, I can always see a strange old man.

He is only about three feet tall. If it weren't for his slightly hunched back, you would never believe he was nearly fifty years old from afar. On his small, wrinkled face, he wears a pair of unusually large glasses. A cluster of Japanese moustache is high on his lips.

Page 18

Almost all year round, he wears the same oil-stained and dusty tailcoat and a top hat with a high crown. However, the high temperature of the tropical region forces him to frequently put it on and take it off. He holds a small cane with an iron head in his other hand, walking solemnly with his head held high and his chest puffed out, as if he were going to a banquet of some celebrities.

On his weak, ridiculous face, there is often a red glow of alcohol. Because he feels that living in Manila is as boring as being in the desert, he often drinks alcohol. However, he does not forget that when he discovers a gentleman-like person from afar, wandering from one end of the square, he quickly straightens his collar, which is almost as charred as coal ash, puts on his top hat, braving the sweat on his head, and walks in the opposite direction, pretending that nothing is happening. When their distance is about twenty feet, he earnestly and solemnly stands aside, a smile floating on the corner of his mouth, bending the hand holding the cane behind his back, and extending the other hand to take off the top hat from his head, tightly贴贴 it to his chest, giving a ninety-degree bow.

"Good morning, sir"!

The one who is called a gentleman will be surprised and frown. They will often suspect that this strange little old man is either drunk or wants to ask him for some "balas" for alms. Some, in order to avoid trouble, will often reach out to take out their wallets. But he will never reach out to receive it immediately. He wants to appear very polite, approaching his face, walking and rambling.

"Sir, you are mistaken, I am not that kind of person..." he says in an apologetic tone, indicating that although he is dilapidated, he still comes from a noble family. "The reason why I am willing to approach you, sir, has a more sacred reason." Then, he coughed lightly, excitedly knocking his cane on the ground. "What I want is not a few balas for alms" he swallowed a mouthful of saliva and said again. "What I want is to tell you, sir, that in this dry desert of Manila, there is still a beautiful flower, and that is Miss Sally. She, a noble Spanish aristocrat and a mixed race of noble Filipino blood; because of poverty, she began to receive her respectable guests. Sir, if you don't mind, you can spend the lowest price to talk to her or do other interesting things..."

For excitement, his face flushed red, and he stared at the small eyes covered by thick glass, looking at the guest. When he finds that the guest is a little bored or wants to leave, he nods frequently and gives a ninety-degree bow.

For curiosity, or for the ridiculous appearance of this old man, bold gentlemen are led to meet his "beautiful flower." And he will be very excited, talking about all kinds of interesting things, or reciting his own glorious past like a recitation. From this, everyone knows that he is also a noble Spanish aristocrat and a mixed race of noble Filipino blood, and that "beautiful flower" is his own biological daughter.

"Before in Nueva Ecija province," he said in a sad tone: "We had a coconut plantation worth two hundred thousand US dollars, but now I have nothing, fifteen years ago, the High Court, at the request of the bank, declared us bankrupt."

They stepped on the small streets of Quiapo, filled with dust, walking windingly for about three or four streets.

Don't Be Greedy for Cheap Things 218

— Elderly Person

"Cheap things are not good," this is a sentence we often hear. Since "cheap" things are not good, we should not be greedy for "cheap" things, especially medicines. It is difficult to have good efficacy when taking cheap medicines, and perhaps adverse effects will occur! Just like the current seasonal cod liver oil, some small pharmacies use low prices to promote sales, but this kind of cheap miscellaneous cod liver oil is not refined well, and its preparation is harmful to the stomach and intestines, so please don't be fooled! So, if you don't buy cod liver oil, you should buy real good cod liver oil, or go to the Five Continents Pharmacy. Because the Five Continents brand of milky white cod liver oil is precisely tested by the blue reaction method, and the vitamin content is rich. The Five Continents Earth brand of malt extract cod liver oil is refined with pure cod liver oil and high-quality malt extract, etc., and the taste is sweet, so the society trusts it the most.

A Small Love Story 219

— Xiulan

Mr. A and his wife have a very good love. One day, after Mr. A's wife put on makeup, Mr. A stood behind her, stroking her hair and said:

"Your cloud-like black hair,

Sprinkled with 'One Three One' hair water,

A gentle breeze blows,

The fragrance permeates the lungs!

I love your cloud-like black hair,

I love that 'One Three One' hair water."

Mr. A's wife smiled happily when she heard these compliments.

(Note) There have always been very few high-quality domestic hair perfumes, and ladies who love to use domestic products generally consider it a pity. Since the advent of the "One Three One" hair perfume from the Five Continents Pharmacy, its fragrance is more elegant than the highest imported products, so now almost all ladies use this kind of hair perfume.

Page 19

, he stopped in front of a basement, valiantly climbed down the扶梯扶梯, let the guests follow behind, and pushed open the door.

In the basement, there was only a narrow room about ten feet long, surrounded by a few simple pieces of furniture, there was a sofa bed, a table, and a cabinet inlaid with a dressing mirror, although it was dark, it was still clean. When the old man entered the door, he called out in a low voice:

"Sally, dear, I brought you guests..."

A half-naked young woman, fat and short, jumped up from the sofa bed like a ball.

"This is Miss Sally, a beautiful flower..." The old man introduced in a touching tone, took the guest's coat, cane or hat, put it in the cabinet, politely gave a bow, retreated to the door, sat on a stone step, smoking a cigarette in his mouth, his head lowered to the ground, ready to hear any cries inside, and went in to serve.

Half an hour later, that door trembled slightly, opened, he was suddenly shocked like he was hit by a stick, hurriedly stood up from the stone steps, retreated to the side and solemnly gave a bow, and said in a low voice:

"Now, sir, please give some money for the wine..."

In less than a quarter of an hour, he appeared in a basement bar, holding a cane in one hand and a top hat in the other, frequently nodding to the people present.

Shopkeeper Liu 220

— Especially

That was when I lived in the east city, I met Shopkeeper Liu.

His age was not very old, but he had a short beard that he had grown quite long. He had the active emotions of an "old young man", often making faces and coaxing the children to laugh when they were having tantrums. If the opportunity arose,—so-called opportunity meant after drinking alcohol—he might even climb on the large kang, a specialty of the north, let the children ride on his back, while hummming on his back, his big buttocks would constantly swing from side to side, like dancing the hula.

Of course, it was not just a little bit like that. The north's large courtyard has quite a large horizontal area. The sun sets on the west wall, and the children living in the courtyard all set out on their way. It's not as good as everyone liked to play hide-and-seek at that time, and it was extremely important to be fair to the person who was hiding. For this, he would also sit lightly on the stone platform with his big buttocks, acting as the judge of fairness. There was a period when they got tired of playing hide-and-seek and switched to "leading the dragon's head" (also called the old eagle catching chickens). In order to protect the small creatures behind the dragon's head, the position of "head" was very tight, and this role, of course, belonged to him.

This house with three courtyards was pawned by him with more than two years of hard work. The owner of the house was from another village and had been empty for several months, unable to rent it out. However, the old man who guarded the house needed a few dollars a month to get rid of him. Later, because he was waiting to repay the debt, our Shopkeeper Liu pawned it at a very small price. One pawn was for ten years! What is worth thanking is that it was this pawn that gave us the opportunity to live together and to recognize his face.

Shopkeeper is a collective name for small-scale businesses in the north, like the southerners call the boss. He opened a "oil and salt shop" with two door-faces directly opposite where we lived. This kind of shop can't be seen in Shanghai. Its nature includes most of what people call the "seven things to open the door," tall counters with some oil, salt, sauce, vinegar, and all kinds of green vegetables, etc. inside. Because in the north, small vegetable markets are rare, so the oil and salt shop took the place of the small vegetable market. Many also partnered with "rice and noodle shops", which naturally gave people more convenience in purchasing.

After that, we gradually came to know the philosophy that Shopkeeper Liu embraced. Because of the relationship in the same courtyard, because of his relationship with the children, his shop became the object of purchase for the same neighbors and nearby. In this way, he easily drove away the other one.

I remember it was spring, when all things were breeding and growing, sparrows were singing harmonious songs in the courtyard, jumping from the tile window to the roof and the treetops, very cute, freedom made them happy, so they were flying in nature. The children could not see these little things. They wanted to catch them, but where could they? Later, they thought of a proper way to catch their cubs from the tiles, raise them, and enjoy them themselves. Soon, this method was passed, but who would catch them? Here, our Shopkeeper Liu took over a burden.

A large tea几几加ded to the eight immortals table, and then a small round stool added to the tea几几. He stood on it, opening his mouth, and stretched his arm into the tiles that sparrows often entered and exited. Suddenly a black thing窜窜 into his mouth, panicked, fell down, his mouth tightly closed, his hand still tightly holding the tail of the black thing, fainted, blood flowed out of his mouth,呵呵 was a small black snake!

Even when I went to Tianjin to study, his throat was not well.

In "Eternal Smile," Hu Die's Three Peking Operas 225

Red Thread Stealing the Box, Yutangchun, Huilong Pavilion

In "Eternal Smile," Hu Die plays a Qinhuai courtesan, who is gentle, beautiful, and passionate.

She is a singer, so in the middle, she sang three operas. At the beginning, while happily playing on Zijin Mountain, she sang "Red Thread Stealing the Box". The following two scenes, "Yutangchun" and "Huilong Pavilion," are all sung in the opera venue.

For these three Peking Operas, Hu Die has been practicing for more than two months. Hu Die originally sang Peking Opera very well, but because she hadn't practiced for a long time, she spent two months practicing these three operas in order to make "Eternal Smile" even more perfect.

The placement of these three operas in "Eternal Smile" is necessary. In her singing, the plot of the play continues to unfold. In her first song, the carriage overturns in the spring field. In her second song, it is fully written how Xu Xinyuan is being fascinated by her. In her third song, it points out who she is singing for.

Chen Yanyan and Tang Guanwu and Fei Boqing in "Heroine of the Lonely City" 226

Lianhua Pictorial Volume 8, Issue 3 Published 227

Lianhua Bookstore's bi-monthly publication, Volume 8, Issue 3, was published on the 16th. The cover of this issue is Chen Yanyan (three-color version), the illustration is Yin Xiucen's Sleep (three-color version), and there are dozens of other copperplate illustrations. It is printed on one hundred reams of copperplate paper. The text pertains to opinions on the film industry's support of the Suiyuan resistance movement, and includes writing from Fei Mu, Sun Yu, Jin Yan, Wang Renmei, Li Mingjian, Cai Chusheng, Li Lili, Han Langan, and Chen Yanyan, etc. Yin Xiucen's Hu Yunjie, Chen Wu, Lingxi, Travelogue, and Lusi are all articles that contribute to the film industry and readers. The price per copy is 8 fen in national currency. All newsstands and bookstores are agents for sales.
